sepezho: workingüëç (reply to 118600)

talkol: I'm following the vote closely and currently the deployed rule is 1 token 1 vote. I think that in this case (where we divide prize money), this is unfair and open to whale manipulation. I have submitted a request to TF to change the tallying mode to 1 wallet 1 vote. I think this is much more fair and will not allow whales to sway the entire vote. The vote is locked on a historic snapshot, so people cannot divide their wallets today to smaller wallets to manipulate.

sepezho: Wouldn't that give bad people an opportunity to run bots that will create wallets and minimally refill them by 1 ton and do voting for a particular project? (reply to 118603)

Max: for this vote no since there is a historic snapshot

talkol: it will save this specific vote from manipulation

talkol: in most other votes, it should always be 1 token 1 vote - because the people with more tokens are impacted more from the result of the vote. But for this case, of hackathon winners, this is not true imo

sepezho: i think the best approach is to lock some tokens for some time - that will be weight of the vote

talkol: so next votes (like the freeze we have last time) would probably stay 1 token 1 vote

talkol: this is what we have now, the votes are on your balance before the vote started (reply to 118608)

talkol: you can't buy tokens to manipulate your voting power

Coalus: what if a bad person is prepared and makes a pool of 1000 wallets, and send 1 TON to each wallet long before the start of voting?  (At the moment, only sufficiently significant voting is being held on this platform, which is why, regardless of the essence of the vote, it can be expensive to be able to lobby for someone's interests) (reply to 118611)

Dario: Or worse, someone prepare 10k wallet (or more) and sold this kind of "service" to anyone who wants to manipulate a public poll (reply to 118612)

talkol: If someone bad was prepared then yes this manipulation will work, but I still think this is less risky than asking whales to vote for you and sharing some prize money with them (reply to 118612)

Dario: In my opinion, its more risky (reply to 118614)

talkol: Who would have been prepared?

Dario: Basically anyone, and then he might sell this service to any other user with interest in it

Dario: Just an bad idea, do not try this at home plz

Tim: You can always check every voter after end to see if he's credible

Tim: no voting system is perfect

Dario: + (reply to 118620)

Tim: if you see that some project in high place have significant number of votes from empty wallets you can disqualify it.

talkol: A lot of the reason we pushed for a community vote for some part of the prize is to make it a little more fair between new projects that were written during the hackathon and older funded projects that raised money before the hackathon and decided to participate because why not get some of the prize.  But what happens now is that funded projects have investors with lots of ton and they are using this ton to make sure they win this part too. This bothers me..

Andrew: not only investors, but big communities that they built long before the hackathon who can vote for them (reply to 118624)

qpwe: Another knight's move from the organizers of the hackathon. The past are described here:  https://t.me/hackatonx/1/6326 (reply to 118625)

Tolya: TON Awards 2022  In 2022 TON Ecosystem has continues an explosive growth started in 2021. Dozens of teams started their commercial and non-commercial projects, created and shared tools and know-hows.  Community grew so big that it became impossible to track all peoples and all projects. Some projects could fall out of sight and did not receive the well-deserved support and promotion.  That is why, in this year we decided to conduct TON Awards: to highlight and encourage the coolest projects in the industry.   In 2022, ecosystem growth outpaced the creation of tools for new projects endorse, but today we have caught up and strongly recommend that new projects to participate in TON Footsteps, TON Grants, TVL Incentivization program, Support for community projects as well as hackatons and dedicated challenges. With this tools we believe funding is much more predictable and transparent, and the need for post factum promotion of research projects will disappear.  Meanwhile, today we honor the daredevils who stepped headlong into the unknown, and relying only on their own strength, laid the foundations of the TON revolution.  Fair rewarding is a difficult task. Our decision was based on the following criteria:  ‚Ä¢ pioneering: to do something that no one has done before you and there are no examples is incredibly difficult, but our winners did it  ‚Ä¢ complexity and volume of work: in the end, diligence rules in the long run  ‚Ä¢ the breadth of the circle of users for whom the project solves the problem  ‚Ä¢ leveling out: some projects have already received funding in one way or another and we encourage projects that support programs have not reached before  ‚Ä¢ non-commerciality: some projects are built to generate income while others, for instance libraries, being very important are hard to be made a product. Thus the latter need more support.  Note, that in TON Award announcements below "Total Awards" is a sum of all support received from TON Foundation in one or another form (including today's reward).  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Seitaro Higuchi)

Tolya: ton-kotlin  Kotlin/Multiplatform SDK for The Open Network.  This is a development by Andrey Pfau before he was invited to the TON core team.  Award: 20 000 TON (~$44 800)  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Tolya)

Tolya: ton3.js & ton-adnl  TON Blockchain low-level API implementation written in TypeScript. ADNL protocol TypeScript implementation for Node.js and Browser context.  Today's Award: 10 000 TON.  10 000 TON was sent earlier in 2022.  Total Award: 20 000 TON (~$44 800)  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Seitaro Higuchi)

Tolya: tonutils-go  Library for work with TON in Golang, focused to be user-friendly, performant and functional in the same time.  Implemented interraction with blockchain and all major TON network protocols, such as: ADNL (TCP+UDP), RLDP, DHT, DNS, RLDP-HTTP, Proxy.  Today's Award: 10 000 TON.  10 000 TON was sent earlier in 2022.  Total Award: 20 000 TON (~$44 800)  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Tolya)

Tolya: TON Proxy Client¬†& TON Reverse Proxy  Cross-playform user-friendly proxy software, implemented natively in Golang, that allows to access TON Sites with end2end encryption without specific knowledge, just run and click 1 button.  Award: 5000 TON¬†(~$11 200)  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Seitaro Higuchi)

Tolya: More from Oleg Baranov:  Documentation with examples about TON internals and protocols: BoC, Merkle Proofs, ADNL (TCP+UDP), DHT, RLDP and other protocols.  Usefull, especially for those who wants to develop their own libraries or low level products in TON.  Will be translated and added to docs.ton.org.  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Tolya)

Oleg Baranov won our hearts and received 17 000 TON (~$38 080) from the personal funds of one of the members of the TON core team.  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Tolya)

Award: 1500 TON (~$3360)  Subsequently, we ordered the development of a jetton-stablecoin FunC smart contract from Dario.  #tonawards2022 (forwarded from Tolya)

Dario: Hi guys! The FunC compiler has a bad behavior and I think its time to find a solution for it. When you define a function, and you dont use it in your code, the compiler doesnt actually removes it from output asm, and this make boc size bigger (and since in ton we pay storage fee, its bad). Now, I think it can be solved by a Fift script, that hiterate over asm output and removes unused functions (by checking code of recv_(internal/external) and ticktock bodies). But fift is hard.
